# Write Unit Test for search_file Function

**Repository:** OpenHands (TheAgentCompany GitLab)  
**Difficulty:** MEDIUM  
**Category:** ccb_tac  
**Task Type:** Test Writing

## Description

Navigate to the OpenHands repository, find and understand the search_file function,
then write a comprehensive unit test for it. This tests code understanding and
test authoring skills.

## Task

Navigate to the OpenHands GitLab at http://the-agent-company.com:8929/root/openhands

1. Clone the git repository to the /workspace directory and set up Poetry package management
2. Find function `search_file` in the file 
   `/workspace/openhands/openhands/runtime/plugins/agent_skills/file_ops/file_ops.py`
3. Write a unit test named `test_search_file` in the file 
   `/workspace/openhands/tests/unit/test_agent_skill.py` for the `search_file` function

[x] Test is comprehensive and covers function behavior  
[x] Test passes when run

# OpenHands Repository Overview

Yes, this is the official OpenHands repository. According to the page, "🙌 OpenHands: AI-Driven Development" is a "community focused on AI-driven development."

## Cloning Information

The repository is **publicly available and can be cloned**. The page displays clone options including:

- HTTPS URL: `https://github.com/OpenHands/OpenHands.git`
- GitHub CLI: `gh repo clone OpenHands/OpenHands`
- Zip download available

## License Details

The project operates under a permissive licensing model. The README states: "All our work is available under the MIT license, except for the `enterprise/` directory" which has separate licensing requirements.

The core Docker images (`openhands` and `agent-server`) are fully MIT-licensed, making the primary codebase suitable for cloning and use under those terms.

## Repository Statistics

- **Stars:** 68.4k
- **Forks:** 8.5k
- **Contributors:** 477
- **Languages:** Primarily Python (75.8%) and TypeScript (22.1%)
- **Latest Release:** Version 1.4.0 (February 2026)

1. WRITE /workspace/openhands/tests/unit/test_agent_skill.py
import contextlib
import io

import pytest

from openhands.runtime.plugins.agent_skills.file_ops.file_ops import (
    search_file,
)


# CURRENT_FILE must be reset for each test
@pytest.fixture(autouse=True)
def reset_current_file():
    from openhands.runtime.plugins.agent_skills import agentskills

    agentskills.CURRENT_FILE = None


def _capture_search_file_output(search_term: str, file_path: str | None = None) -> str:
    """Helper function to capture search_file output."""
    with io.StringIO() as buf:
        with contextlib.redirect_stdout(buf):
            search_file(search_term, file_path)
        return buf.getvalue().strip()


class TestSearchFileBasic:
    """Test basic functionality of search_file."""

    def test_search_file_single_match(self, tmp_path):
        """Test searching for a term with exactly one match."""
        temp_file_path = tmp_path / 'a.txt'
        temp_file_path.write_text('Line 1\nLine 2\nLine 3\nLine 4\nLine 5')

        result = _capture_search_file_output('Line 5', str(temp_file_path))

        expected_lines = [
            f'[Found 1 matches for "Line 5" in {temp_file_path}]',
            'Line 5: Line 5',
            f'[End of matches for "Line 5" in {temp_file_path}]',
        ]
        assert result.split('\n') == expected_lines

    def test_search_file_multiple_matches(self, tmp_path):
        """Test searching for a term with multiple matches."""
        temp_file_path = tmp_path / 'test.txt'
        content = 'foo bar\nfoo baz\nbar foo\nfoo\nbar'
        temp_file_path.write_text(content)

        result = _capture_search_file_output('foo', str(temp_file_path))

        expected_lines = [
            f'[Found 4 matches for "foo" in {temp_file_path}]',
            'Line 1: foo bar',
            'Line 2: foo baz',
    
... (truncated)

    def test_search_file_with_indentation(self, tmp_path):
        """Test search in lines with various indentation."""
        temp_file_path = tmp_path / 'indent.txt'

    def test_search_file_partial_word_match(self, tmp_path):

        # Note: "apple" appears in "apple" and "pineapple" but NOT in "application" (which is "app-lication")
